# 道门通教必用集

**Daoist Canon of Universal Teachings: A Comprehensive Collection**

**Title:** *Daoist Canon of Universal Teachings: A Comprehensive Collection*
**Original Attribution:** Compiled by Lü Taigu of the Song dynasty
**Volume:** Nine fascicles
**Source Edition:** *Zhengtong Daozang* (Orthodox Daoist Canon), Section One

  - *Preface to the Daoist Comprehensive Teachings Collection* (道门通教集序)

The Celestial Master established his teachings in the Western Shu, while Guangcheng attained final repose in Yizhou, hence the people of Shu revered the Dao in great splendor and observed its rites meticulously.

Upon examining the traditions passed down by the various lineages, it was found that there were no authoritative editions, and errors were indeed numerous.

Recently, observing the completion of the Zhongzang Canon, I encountered Liu Gong of the Left History Bureau and Zhu Gong of the Tai Chang Office, both officials in the capital. Li Gong of the Two Rivers, a disciple of the Master of the Daoist Lineage, requested that I obtain several hundred Daoist scriptures from the capital, all of which were texts missing from Shu.

Among them, ritualistic liturgy was predominant, so I commissioned Master Taigu to compare and reconcile their differences, to examine antiquity and distinguish the present.

From the foundational teachings for novices to the advanced rites of practice, he meticulously compiled them into a collection for the benefit of future generations, coinciding with my tenure as the Yellow Arrow Register of the Two Rivers.

Scholars and practitioners from all directions gathered in homage, and thus the texts were engraved upon wooden tablets for all to share.

I have often lamented my inability to contribute, as some merely stand by with folded arms, while others mock or even suppress these teachings, unwilling to utter a single word to my disciples.

Is this not contrary to the Celestial Master’s intent, which was to foster growth and abundance? If the Daoist lineage lacks scriptures, should not those who share this vision strive to emulate the spirit of Zhengyi and Guangcheng, thereby upholding the grand tradition?

In the summer of the year *Jiaxu* of the *Jiatai* era, Master Lü Yuansu of Jiangyuan, the recluse of the Northern Peak, composed this work.

In ancient times, the Son of Heaven sacrificed to Heaven and Earth, communing with the divine, all with solemn rites—pure offerings, meticulous attire, preliminary fasting, and then the full observance, lest the ritual fail to honor the spirits and the sacrifice be incomplete. How much more so for commoners?

Thus, the Celestial Master expounded the scriptures and established precepts, prioritizing compassion over killing. Following this, the Celestial Master established his teachings, transforming sacrifices into *zhaijiao* rites, mirroring Heaven and Earth, offering reverence, reciting scriptures, and dispatching talismans to convey prayers, all to elevate grand rituals and refine pure sacrifices.

Therefore, hymns and odes were composed to praise the Daoist temples, where words became music, and it was said that sound could reach the divine, invoking blessings from above and below. The *Changxu* (recitation of talismans) and *Yongdong* (chanting of scriptures) were derived from this principle, and their essence was unchanging.

Since the Celestial Master’s establishment of his teachings, those among the Daoist lineage who focused on ritualistic precepts often neglected the study of sound, while those who mastered sound often lacked the full complement of ritualistic observances.

This is akin to Gongshu Bu’s skill—without the compass and square, how could he measure the perfect circles and squares?

In the Song dynasty, the Lü family of Helin compiled the Daoist scriptures, gathering their mysteries into a collection they titled *The Comprehensive Teachings Collection* (通教集).

From the imperial court to the common folk, for the sake of the nation, the family, the living, and the dead, those who practiced *zhao* (ritual fasting) and *jiao* (exorcism) revered Daoist teachings universally, all finding partial illumination.

It was also to ensure that students of the Dao would master the precepts through ritualistic discipline, thereby comprehending its teachings. His intent was indeed broad.

He Gong of Yuntai further elucidated these principles, enabling practitioners to refine and master the rituals, and compiled *The Refined Teachings Collection* (炼教集), which has since circulated widely.

Within these two collections, there are mutual strengths and weaknesses, and those who study them cannot help but raise questions.

Now, Master Ma Daoyi of Jincheng’s Three Wells Observance, who has long resided among the Daoist elite, has devoted years to the study of ritualistic texts without ever abandoning them.

Thus, he merged *The Comprehensive Teachings Collection* (通教集) and *The Refined Teachings Collection* (炼教集), selecting their finest elements, categorizing them into a single volume, and engraved it for wider dissemination.

He entrusted me with a preface to explain his purpose. I replied: In matters of scholarship, I have always taken care. Within the realm of ritual teachings, my knowledge has been neglected for many years.

Yet you have taken this as a teaching, and I dare not fail to encourage its completion for the sake of its beauty.

Students of the Dao may use this to understand its standards, and those with noble aspirations may practice it to commune with the divine.

This is indeed a grand event for the Daoist lineage—who could not rejoice in it?

In the mid-autumn of the *Yuan Zheng* year, Master Han Hongcheng, the Senior Lecturer of Ren’an Observance and the Great Master of Proliferating the Dao and Awakening to Truth, respectfully composed this preface.

**Essential for the Daoist Comprehensive Teachings Collection (通教集):**
At the outset of seeking the Dao, one must first seek its standards. Those who take vows must possess the complete scriptures and precepts.

From the Han dynasty to the present, all who upheld the lineage and established teachings followed the Celestial Master’s model, and their practices can serve as exemplary standards. Thus, the first section is established as *Standards of the Celestial Master*:

- *Scriptures and Precepts of the Celestial Master’s Ascetic Life*
- *Brief Biographies of Successive Masters*

For novices entering the Dao, the hymns of response must come first, from the *Opening Hall* to the *Farewell to the Sage*, all can be praised and recorded in the ritual scriptures.

At the beginning of initiation, one may lack a good edition, hence the second section is established as *Verbal Praises*:

- *Words of the Step-into-Void Rite and Praises*
- *True-Writing Talismans for Invoking All Kinds of Perfected Ones*
- *True-Writing Talismans for Disaster Dispersion in the Five Directions*
- *Twelve Vows of Mindful Retention*

---

「As the child grows into maturity, instruction in phonetics and metrics follows, with single-tone recitation and chanting to assist in ritual practice. Yet errors in transmission and repetition may lead to crude and unrefined imitation—all such flaws must be corrected to achieve precision and solemnity. Thus, the third section is established as *Chants and Praises*:

- *Five-Directional Protective Spirits' Incantations*

Inner and outer ritual affairs are not confined to a single path—some texts may be incomplete, and some originals may contain errors. For beginners, caution is advised, selecting the best and following it. Thus, the fifth section is established as *Assistants and Praises*:

- *Three-Day Lamentation Scripture*
- *Yellow Arrow Rite Petitions and Repentance for Dispersal*

The above eight sections are all drawn from Daoist scriptural canons and meticulously examined through the teachings of past masters and renowned scholars of recent times. Compiled into one volume, no presumption is made, lest later sages be misled. If kept as a private family secret, it would not be a universal doctrine. Therefore, it is engraved upon wood to share with fellow students, serving as an essential guide for transmitting the Dao and saving others.

Do not lightly impart this to uninitiated laypersons, lest you invite regret. For if this collection is even slightly comprehensive, they may abandon their original path, devoting themselves to this instead—only to meet ruin later, inviting censure and blame.

As for the profound teachings of Laozi and Zhuangzi, or the methods of Golden Elixir cultivation, those who follow the Dao must each have their share. This is not the Dao’s presence in the world, but rather the imperial institutional framework. The enlightened will surely recognize this truth.

Composed in the late summer of the *Xinyou* year of the *Jiatai* era (1201) by the Daoist Lu Taigu of Hèlín Yuan, a native of Jiàn’ān.

**Volume One of the *Daoist Universal Teachings Collection***
**Lu Taigu’s *Hèlín Collection***
**The *Jīnshì* Chapter**
**The *Tàishàng Out-Home Sutra Instructions***

The *Sutra of the Causes and Conditions for Leaving Home* states: The Daoists have seven stages in total. The Celestial Venerable says:

1. **Celestial Purity**—that is, the body harmonizes with Nature, and the inner and outer are perfectly tranquil.
2. **Divine Immortals**—that is, transformations beyond measure, transcending the realm of the ordinary.
3. **Secluded Elegance**—that is, containing light and hiding brilliance, unburdened by worldly entanglements.
4. **Mountain Dwellers**—that is, secluded in study of the Dao, with wisdom and benevolence naturally at ease.
5. **Those Who Leave Home**—that is, abandoning all attachments to the world, casting off the dust and clamor of mortal life.
6. **Those Who Remain in the World**—that is, blending with the world’s light, embracing the Dao and nurturing virtue.
7. **Sacrificial Attendants**—that is, humbling oneself among the vulgar, rescuing and delivering those in peril.

Thus, the term *Daoist* refers to one who, in all actions—moving, standing, sitting, or lying down—every thought and intention is devoted solely to cultivating the Dao and attending to virtue. They observe fasts and pay homage, chant scriptures and burn incense, uphold precepts and refine their conduct, light lamps for repentance, make offerings with sincere vows, expound the Great Vehicle, and guide all beings. They awaken the great mind of the Dao, create boundless merit, benefit all without distinction, and always place others before themselves, free from worldly toil. Their sole pursuit is the Dao’s work, and thus they are revered as the most exalted among the Six Paths and Fourfold Existence—both heavenly and earthly. They do not bow to the Son of Heaven nor salute the feudal lords, becoming fields of blessing for humankind and the refuge for the Three Realms.

The **Seventeen Vows of Daoist Aspiration for Leaving Home and Attaining the True Body**:
1. I vow never to kill living beings, for it severs the sacred lineage.
2. I vow forever to abstain from alcohol, for it corrupts pure nature.
3. I vow forever to abstain from blood, for it defiles the body.
4. I vow not to consume the five pungent herbs, for they obstruct the paths of Heaven and Earth.
5. I vow not to indulge in lustful desires, for they disturb the mind.
6. I vow not to speak of others’ faults, for it invites hatred.
7. I vow not to covet wealth, for it hinders the Dao.
8. I vow to diligently cultivate merit, for it adorns oneself.
9. I vow not to disturb or anger others, for it breeds karmic enmity.
10. I vow to benefit others without hesitation, for it is no different from benefiting myself.
11. I vow forever to speak no falsehoods, for it makes others distrustful.
12. I vow never to grow weary or negligent, for it dulls the resolve of the Dao.
13. I vow to study all methods with effort, for it ripens the wisdom of the seed.
14. I vow never to steal from others, for it demands double repayment.
15. I vow to always observe inner fasting, for it attains pure harmony of mind.
16. I vow to constantly reflect upon the emptiness and tranquility of all dharmas, for it swiftly advances the Dao.
17. I vow to always be humble and silent as the foolish, for it ensures inner peace.

All the above vows are upheld by novices who enter the Dao.

The *Sutra of Ascending the Mysterious* states: The Daoist’s conduct is entirely opposite to that of the common person. Their eyes do not gaze excessively, nor are they startled by beauty. Their ears do not listen to slander nor to chaotic sounds. Their noses do not inhale fragrant scents, nor do they relish the pungent stench of decay. Their mouths do not crave sweetness, nor do they consume what violates all life. Their hearts do not dwell on desires, whether for wealth, sensual pleasures, or honor. Their hands do not act deceitfully, nor do their feet tread upon evil.

The *Sutra of Ascending the Mysterious* also states: All who leave home must discard ornamentation and fine attire, wearing only coarse cloth and simple garments, dwelling in lowly beds and modest huts—merely to sustain their bodies. They must not indulge in luxury. Except for treating illness or traveling, they may not seek permission to go outside. They must reside in clean, secluded places, indulging in the Dao’s subtle and boundless joys. This is called the **threshold of hearing the Dao** and the **foundation of great virtue**.

The *Sutra of Fixing the Will* states: In the past, there was a youth of twelve who lived in idle pleasure, preparing fine food together, drinking deeply and reveling in games. Sometimes they would debate whether the practice of the Dao and the upholding of precepts were difficult or easy. The Celestial Venerable, in great tranquility, perceived them and knew that in their previous lives, each had been a teacher to others, hoarding scriptures and grudgingly sharing them, causing their disciples to hesitate. Now, they had fallen into the dust of the world through this slight cause, yet still could be saved. The Celestial Venerable then transformed into a mortal man, passing through their gathering and overhearing their conversation. The man said: *"Upholding precepts is very easy; not upholding them is far more difficult."* The youth, hearing this, asked in unison: *"How so, sir? You say upholding precepts is easy, yet not upholding them is difficult?"* The man replied: *"Standing upright like a precept is easy—one need not fear the Son of Heaven nor the spirits and gods. But breaking a precept is difficult: such a person fears all mortals and fears the spirits and gods even more. How could it not be difficult?"* Thus, the twelve youth, upon hearing the man’s words, all recalled their past lives, resolved to uphold precepts, and together attained the fruit of the Dao.

The *Sutra of the Dharma Wheel* states: The Celestial Venerable of Oneness and Mystery instructed Ge Xian Gong, saying: *"In my past, I received my teacher’s instruction with utmost severity. The lessons cut deep as a knife, stung like a poisoned thorn. I bowed and knelt in service, never daring to slacken, never daring to refuse the pain or speak of the poison. Now that I have attained the fruit of the Dao, I cannot repay my teacher’s kindness."*

The *Great True Precepts* state: Daoists must first master the **Five Thousand Characters** of scriptural study. They must expound and comprehend the teachings, guide others, and benefit themselves, opening boundless enlightenment. This is the mark of the **Great Vehicle Practitioner**.

The *Great True Precepts* also state: At the dawn of creation, the **Sage-True Immortals** all proclaimed the Dao’s *qi* and established laws, passing them down through generations. They shared the same lineage as the Celestial Venerable, all called **Learned Masters**. Their work was the Dao, and their devotion to the Dao bore fruit, earning them the title of *Daoist*.

The *Sutra of Illuminating the Threat* states: **Study must never be superficial**, for false and true teachings may appear similar. One must not fail to discern them, for failure leads to perilous paths, while clarity grants ease. The difference between clarity and obscurity lies in the mind’s careful examination. The method of discernment is to **pervasively study all scriptures**, test them through experience, and verify their truth. Thus, one naturally attains luminous understanding—whether of worldly or transcendent laws, of actions with or without purpose. One will naturally fathom the subtleties of the **Three Pure Ones**.

**Brief Transmission of the Lineage Across Generations**:
The Daoist teachings are ancient. **Huangdi and Laozi** championed the Way of **Purity and Stillness**. The disciples **Yin Ling, Zhang Tao, Lie Yukou, and Zhuangzi** expanded upon it, and the tradition flowed down to **Le Su Gong**. Gong taught **Ge Xian Gong**, and Ge Xian Gong taught **Cao Can**.

The efficacy of these words in governing the world is as described—how much more so the Dao of **Huang-Lao**!

Alas, the world now indulges in extravagance and excess, and thus this Way grows hidden. The study of **immortality and transcendence** flourishes, and rites of supplication and sacrifice thrive. From the Eastern Han onward, until the beginning of the **Sui Dynasty**, **Pengqiuzi Jia Shanheng** and over a hundred others proclaimed this Way to the world, compiling *The High Dao Transmission*. From these, I have selected the most distinguished ten or so, distilling their essence and appending them to the scriptural teachings, so that my disciples may know whom to emulate and revere.

**Zhang Tian师**
Tian师 bore the surname Zhang, given name **Dao Ling**, and courtesy name **Fu Han**. By nature, he was silent and revered antiquity, mastering both scriptures and histories while also excelling in **celestial omens and divination**. He relieved the urgent needs of others without distinction of familiarity or distance, and thus the world esteemed him, drawing many to his discipleship. When the **Emperor Zhang** summoned him, he declined, sighing as he parted from his disciples—only **Wang Chang** remained to attend him. He then retreated to **Qian** and **Heng**, reaching **Zhongyue Mountain**, where he obtained the **Nine Elixir Scriptures**. Upon refining the elixir, he told Chang: *"I have yet to fulfill a great deed—how dare I hastily consume it? I must first benefit the state and family, eliminating harm and promoting good, before I may act lightly."* Thus, he moved the **Celestial Sovereign** to descend, granting him the **All-One Alliance and Awe** methods, subduing the **hosts of demons and jade maidens**, and establishing **twenty-four administrative precincts**. He taught people to confess sins and apportion blessings, instituting systematic precepts. The people of Shu were transformed, abandoning vice and fleeing crime. Later, upon **Yuntai Peak**, the Celestial Sovereign dispatched a **cloud-chariot** to descend and welcome him, and he ascended to heaven in broad daylight.

**Ge Xian Gong**
Xian Gong bore the surname Ge, given name **Xuan**, and courtesy name **Xiao Xian**. From his youth, he loved learning, mastering all **scriptures, histories, and classics**, and his fame spread across the **Jiangzuo region**. He often played the zither and recited **Zhuangzi and Laozi**, content and serene, needing nothing within. He then entered **Chicheng Mountain** to cultivate the Dao, later wandering through **Kuaiyang, Luofulou, Jinjing, Hezao, Yushi, and Tiantai Mountains**, refining his practice and recitations. Thus, he was visited by the **Three Pure Ones of the Supreme Polarity**, who bestowed upon him the **Three Cavern Treasure Scriptures**. At eighteen, he achieved Dao-completion, his transformations beyond measure. He compiled the essentials of the Three Caverns into the *Nine Abyssal Confessions* and authored over ten volumes on **Laozi and other scriptures**. One day, he told his disciples **Zheng Siyuan** and others: *"The Wu ruler detains me, preventing me from reciting the Cavern Scriptures. I must first achieve **corpse dissolution**, then ascend to heaven."* When the time came, his body softened like silk, filling the room with fragrant qi. By the fifth day, a great wind arose, extinguishing all lamps. When the fire was lit, his corpse had vanished.

**Wang Zuan**
The Daoist **Wang Zuan** resided on **Maji Mountain**, often performing **meritorious deeds in secret** to save others. During the late **Western Jin**, as the Central Plains fell into chaos, famine, pestilence, and disease ravaged the people, many perishing without relief. Moved by pity, Zuan composed a **petition in seclusion**, weeping profusely. After three nights, light filled his chamber as at noon. Soon, auspicious winds and clouds gathered in the sky, strange fragrances and celestial music descended to his courtyard, accompanied by **banners and flags**, **green boys and jade maidens**, and **dragons and tigers** as guards. Suddenly, the sounds of **mouth organs and flutes** came from the northwest. Amidst five-colored light, a **celestial official** announced to Zuan: *"The Dao Sovereign of the Celestial Sovereign arrives."* A **treasure-seat** then descended from the sky, and the Dao Sovereign took his place. Zuan knelt and prostrated himself before him. The Dao Sovereign said: *"You pitied the living, your petition sincere, your heart laid bare—this moved both the seen and unseen. The earthly officials have reported you, and I have come to observe."* The Dao Sovereign then expounded on **the cycles of yin and yang**, the **ascents and descents of humans and spirits**, the **Six Heavens’ demons and fallen generals**, who preyed on the weak, seizing opportunities to harm the living. *"I have subdued them with solar might and divine incantations, and their chaos has naturally ceased."* He then commanded his attendants to grant Zuan the **Scriptures of Divine Transformation and Divine Incantations**, along with the **Three-Five Fast Precepts**, saying: *"Diligently practice these—true stages may yet be attained."* As Zuan traveled through **Jiangbiao**, the plagues ceased.

**Lu Tian师**
Lu **Xiujing**, courtesy name **Yuande**,

The Dao Sovereign said: *"Your steadfast devotion to tombs and classics, your wide exploration of symbols and celestial omens—this is admirable. Yet you sighed, declaring: 'I wish to refine my form and merge with the Dao, to attain harmony with Heaven and complete my destiny, but this is not what you mean.' Thus, you devoted yourself exclusively to Daoist teachings, never ceasing in your studies, even in sleep. When you heard of a master of strange arts, though distant, you would seek them out. Dwelling in the rugged peaks of Jing, the people of Jiang and Han would come to listen, arriving empty-handed but returning with true understanding.

By the end of the Song dynasty’s **Yuanjia** era, Emperor Wen could not summon you. But when Emperor Ming ascended, desiring to bring **purity and stillness** to guide the people toward simplicity and sincerity, he deeply admired you. Thus, he repeatedly invited you, and you finally accepted the imperial command to descend from the mountains. Bears, tigers, monkeys, and birds lamented along the road, their sorrowful cries echoing—such was your influence on all things.

Upon reaching the capital, you were lodged in a guesthouse outside the palace gates, allowing both officials and commoners to receive instruction from you. You then clarified the distinctions between **heresy and orthodoxy**, examining and verifying the authenticity of teachings. From this, the corrupt customs of the age transformed in unison. You once blended the **Three Caverns’ scriptures and methods**, but later corrected and refined them.

You also composed **rituals for fasting and purification**, establishing them as enduring precepts for future generations. Your friendship with **Tao Yuanming**, a fellow **outsider to formal ranks**, reveals much of your character.

In the fifth year of **Yuanhui**, on the first month, you suddenly told your disciples: 'I am pressed by imperial favor, forced to abandon my lifelong resolve. Now I shall return to my old mountain retreat.' Your disciples were astonished. On the second day of the third month, you quietly ascended, your skin radiant and luminous, a fragrant scent lingering in the air. Three days later, your disciples on Lushan saw a carriage adorned with **rainbow-colored banners**, and in an instant, you vanished, returning to your former abode.

The emperor posthumously conferred the title **Simple and Tranquil Master** upon you.

**Kao Tian师**
**Kao Qianzhi**, courtesy name **Fuzhen**,

At eighteen, he devoted himself wholeheartedly to the Dao, his spirit subtly attuned to the **Supreme Mysteries**. There was a **Celestial Master**, Cheng Gongxing, who took him as a servant in his household. One day, as Kao Qianzhi calculated the **cosmic resonances** of the **Five Phases** and **Six Qi**, he found the **Celestial Patterns** misaligned. Gongxing instructed him, and with a single adjustment, it was perfected. After some time, Gongxing said to him: *"The Daoist Master has the will to cultivate the Way—perhaps you and I may withdraw together."* He then took him to **Hua Mountain**, where they gathered herbs for sustenance. From that point on, Qianzhi never again felt hunger. One day, he said: *"I shall depart, but someone will bring you medicine."* He ate it, and indeed, it was as he had spoken. Upon examining the herbs, they were foul and venomous—poisonous creatures and noxious substances. He grew fearful and left. Gongxing returned and explained, sighing: *"The Daoist Master is not yet ready for transcendence, but he may become a teacher for kings."* He added: *"I shall depart tomorrow."* True to his word, he ascended at the appointed time. Qianzhi then settled in **Songyang**, never emerging again.

In the second year of **Shenrui**, on the first day of the fourth month, two men suddenly arrived, riding dragons and bearing **auspicious banners**, declaring: *"The **Celestial Worthy** has come."* In an instant, the **Most High** descended in a **Nine-Dragon Jade Chariot**, surrounded by divine attendants, gathering atop the mountain. Qianzhi bowed in reverent devotion. The **Most High** commanded **Wang Fangping** to bring Qianzhi forward, saying: *"I have received the **Celestial Register of the Central Peak’s Gathering of Immortals**, which states that since **Zhang Daoling** attained **True Perfection**, those who cultivate the Way have lacked a true teacher. Now there is the **Daoist of the Central Peak, Kao Qianzhi**, whose conduct aligns with **Natural Principle**. He should be placed in the **Master’s rank**, and thus I entrust you with the **Celestial Master’s mission**, along with the **Cloud-Middle Chanting**—the **Precious Scripture of the **Harmonious Precepts** and the **Newly Codified **Void-Wandering** Rituals**. You must proclaim them, assist the empire, and transform the people."* After Qianzhi accepted, the **Five-Cloud Platform Hall** vanished. From then on, his resolve and conduct grew ever more refined.

During the **Shiji** era, the imperial court sent officials to summon him to the capital. **Sima Chengzhi**, the **Grand Tutor**, became his disciple, and the emperor himself knelt before him, asking questions with the utmost reverence. A **Celestial Altar** was erected in his honor, and thus the entire realm turned to him in veneration. The **Celestial Master** once performed rites at the **Central Peak** for the emperor’s blessings, and through his profound sincerity, the **Most High** secretly bestowed upon the emperor the title **Emperor of True Peace**. That year, the era was renamed **True Peace, First Year**.

By the ninth year, he told his disciples: *"I dreamed of Cheng Gongxing, who summoned me to the **Celestial Palace of the Central Peak**."* In the fifth month, he **ascended in spirit**, with a **green vapor** like mist emanating from his mouth, rising to the heavens before dissipating. His body gradually shrank, and those who understood it called it **corpse dissolution**. He lived to eighty-four. Later, **Shen You** saw him atop the **Central Peak**, his body radiant silver, shining like the sun—thus proving him to be an **Immortal**.

---

**Celestial Master Wang Daoyi**
Wang Daoyi, a **Daoist** of the **Wei Dynasty**, was well-versed in all scriptures and mastered the **divinatory classics**. Learning of the **Empress Yin’s retreat** at **Zhongnan**, he came with six or seven disciples to dwell there, joining **Daoist Yin Lingjian** and forty others in spreading the **Great Dao’s transformation**. Though times were famine-stricken and provisions scarce, Daoyi expanded the **observatory halls** with hundreds of artisans, yet expenses never faltered. All knew it was due to the **Master’s divine influence**, as if secretly aided by the **Celestial**. Thus, every **pavilion and hall** was renewed.

He ordered his disciples to gather **True Scriptures**, amassing over ten thousand volumes—all through his own efforts, never seeking aid from others. His nature was boundless and unencumbered; even in his inner chambers, those who eavesdropped on his disciples found only **gathered Immortals** in speech. During the **Yongping** era, as he was about to **ascend**, white clouds and strange fragrances filled the room, lingering for days. A villager returning from afar saw Daoyi depart riding a **deer**.

---

**Master of Rectification, Sima Chengzhen**
Sima Chengzhen, courtesy name **Zimwei**, served **Pan Shizheng** and mastered the **Alchemy of the Form**. His teacher, recognizing his extraordinary nature, fully transmitted the **Dao of Tao Yuanming’s Rectification**. After some time, he declined and wandered the sacred peaks. Arriving at **Tiantai**, he built a **multi-tiered pavilion** on the altar, naming it the **Pavilion of Universal Marvels**.

The **Empress Wu** summoned him, but he soon departed. He was counted among the **Ten Friends of the Daoist Sect**, alongside **Chen Zhi’ang, Lu Zangyong, Song Zhiwen, Wang Shi, Bi Gou, Li Bai, Meng Haoran, Wang Wei, and He Zhizhang**.

The **Emperor Ruizong** summoned him again, commanding his brother **Sima Chengyi** to deliver the imperial edict, insisting he come. Upon arrival, he was led into the **inner palace**, where the emperor questioned him on his arts. The Master replied: *"Cultivating the Dao is daily subtraction, until one reaches **non-being**—what the vulgar eyes and ears perceive. Each subtraction is already difficult; how much more so to attack heterodoxies and inflate one’s cleverness?"*

The emperor asked: *"This applies to refining one’s self, but how does it govern the realm?"*
The Master answered: *"The realm is but an extension of the self. Thus, one must **harmonize the mind with stillness**, **blend the qi with emptiness**, let **things follow their nature**, and abandon all **private scheming**—then the realm will be governed."*

The emperor sighed: *"The words of **Broad-Nurturing Child**!"*
He then requested permission to return to the mountains, receiving a **jewel-veined lute** and a **cloud-patterned robe** as gifts. The emperor ordered officials to compose poems in farewell.

The **Emperor Xuanzong** decreed the construction of **altars and chambers** on **Wangwu Mountain** for his residence. At that time, **Jiao Jingzhen**, a **Female Immortal** of the **Mohe**, sailed to **Penglai** in search of a teacher. Upon reaching a mountain, she was told by a **Daoist** that *"Sima Zimwei of Tiantai Mountain is renowned in the **Jade Hall**, dwelling in **Chicheng**—he is truly a noble teacher."* Jingzhen returned to receive the Dao from the Master and soon ascended.

Once, descending to speak with **Xue Jichang**, he said: *"The Master has attained the Dao higher than **Tao Dunshui**; he shall become the **Eastern Heaven’s Pure and Clear True Person**."* One day, the Master suddenly told his **grass-clad disciples**: *"From the **Jade Mist Peak’s east**, I see **Penglai’s** Immortals descending. Now the **Eastern Heaven’s Green Boy Lord** summons me—I must go."* In an instant, he ascended.

The emperor posthumously honored him as **Silver Green Light-Lucre Grand Official**, with the posthumous title **Master of Rectification**. The emperor himself inscribed his stele.

Among his works, the *Secrets of True Cultivation*, *Diagram of the Celestial Treasury*, *Treatise on Sitting-Forgetting*, and *System of Ascension* circulate in the world.

Li Han Guang
The Daoist Li Han Guang, at the age of thirteen, was deeply devoted to Daoist learning. Though in seclusion, he conducted himself as if before sovereign and father. Skilled in seal and clerical scripts, men praised him as surpassing his own father. Once he heard the Dao, he never again engaged in worldly affairs.

His master, Master Sima Zhengyi, upon seeing him, declared: *"He is indeed a guest of the True Celestial Purity."* He admonished him: *"Hold fast to emptiness, accumulate no attachments, and your Way shall know no end. Entrust yourself to the hidden peaks and efface your traces—your virtue is profound."* Thus, he entrusted him with all his sacred texts, bidding him first save others.

Han Guang, having received this teaching, forgot himself in the Dao and aided others in their needs. Whenever he conducted rituals, he purified his heart and body without slacking. The Tang Emperor Minghuang summoned him to inquire about his practices, and he replied: *"The Dao De Jing is the sovereign’s teacher. When the Han Emperor Wen practiced it, he elevated the people to benevolent longevity."*

The emperor further asked about the Golden Cauldron, and he answered: *"The Dao and its virtue are public. Lightness of action is private within the public—if one seeks life while indulging desires, it is like harnessing the wind; how difficult!"*

The emperor praised him and treated him with great honor. Soon after, Han Guang requested to return to Jùqū. The emperor established the Zǐyáng Observatory for his residence.

When the emperor received the *True Scripture of Blessings and Auspiciousness*, he again requested Han Guang as his teacher, but he declined, offering his refusal from the Dàtóng Hall. The emperor posthumously honored him as **Master Xuánjìng**, and his works *The Transmission of Immortal Learning* and *On the Differences and Similarities of the Celestial Mysteries* circulate in the world.

At eighty-seven, he told his disciples: *"I shall go to Mount Mao."* He then ascended in due time, with auspicious clouds descending and elixir grasses sprouting. His rank was that of an Immortal Official of Mount Mao.

Wu Zongyuan
Wu Jun, styled **Zhēnjié**,

「Mastered the *Classics of Dao* and refined eloquent prose. Though he failed to pass the *Jìnshì* examinations, he departed to dwell at Yǐdì Mountain. In the early years of *Tiānbǎo*, he was summoned to the capital, where he petitioned to be enrolled among the *Daoists*, studying under Master Pàn Shīzhèng. He journeyed south to *Tiāntái*, gazed upon the *Cānghǎi*, and consorted with eminent scholars, whose literary works spread back to the capital.

Emperor *Mínghuáng* summoned him and conversed with great delight, commanding him to serve as a *Hànlín* scribe and presenting him with three essays on the *Xuángāng*. The emperor inquired about the Dao, and he replied: *"None surpass Laozi in profound understanding of the Dao; Your Majesty may seek it within the *Wǔqiān Wén*."* When further questioned about the arts of *shénxiān* (immortals) and alchemical cultivation, he answered: *"This is the concern of rustics, not of a sovereign—it is unwise for rulers to dwell upon such matters."*

Yet whenever he spoke, his discourse centered on *orthodox teachings* and worldly affairs, employing subtle language to admonish and advise. The emperor held him in high regard. The *Sāmén* (Buddhist monks) resented his favor, and *Gāolìshì*, who had long served the *Fútóu* (Buddhist) sect, together defamed him before the emperor. He then requested to return to *Sōngshān*, and the emperor decreed the establishment of a pavilion for him.

He expounded on the *mysteries of the Grain Spirit* (*Gǔshén*), producing *The Treatise on the Xuángāng*. Mournful for the *blue-pine heart* and *withered gaze* of those distant from the Dao, he wrote *The Treatise on Immortality as a Learnable Art*. He composed *The Heart-Washing Ode* and *The Éxī Retreat Ode* to clarify the *transcendent purity* and *liberation from worldly entanglements*. His works on cultivating sincerity within the chest to rest in *Tianjūn* (Celestial Balance) include *The Theory of Heart and Mind* and *The Hymn of Divine Accord*. His poems on *wandering among immortals*, *treading the void*, and *mixed reflections on royal governance* total over four hundred and fifty, collected and prefaced by *Guān Déyǔ*.

Later, he attained *spiritual dissolution*, and the emperor posthumously honored him as **Master Zōngyuán**. His works were compiled by **Liú Zhīgǔ**, styled **Xiānxián** (Celestial Hidden), a native of *Pèi*. A descendant of the *Zhèng King of Zhōngshān*, his ancestors served as officials in *Línqióng*, and the family settled there. His mother, of the *Hào* clan, conceived him after a divine dream, and she was endowed with wisdom and virtue, taking no delight in worldly gain or fame. She devoted herself solely to the Dao, later joining the *Tàiqīng Guān* (Great Clarity Monastery) and receiving the *sāndòng jīnglù* (triple cave scriptures and talismans).

She mastered the *Bāgōng Bǎozhāng* (Eight Immortals’ Precious Scriptures), the *sāndòng bǎolù* (triple cave talismans), the *Dānjīng Màijué* (Alchemical Canon of Veins and Pulse), and the *shēngshēng rùsǐ* (methods of birth-and-death transcendence), all without exception. The *Ruìzōng* emperor summoned him for inquiry, and his Daoist attainments pleased the sovereign, who bestowed special honors upon him before he returned to his mountain.

During the *Kāiyuán* era, he was summoned again to alleviate the people’s suffering. As a *Zhēnrén* (True Person), he observed the *yùsè* (color of the complexion) and *dàimài* (pulse), dispersing *qì* to remove ailments. Eighteen out of every ten people benefited and found peace. The emperor’s gifts he declined, instead requesting permission to return to *Shù* (Sichuan), and he was granted a decree to establish his residence as the *Dàqiānqiū Guān* (Great Thousand Autumns Monastery). The emperor inscribed the name himself, and **Lǐ Yōng** composed the stele.

Later, during the *Tiāncháng Jié* (Heavenly Length Festival), the monastery was renamed *Tiāncháng Guān* (Heavenly Length Monastery), and further arrangements were made for its expansion. When visitors came, he imparted the *Huángbái shù* (elixir arts of gold and silver). Though their dwellings were grand and splendid, costing tens of thousands, he never relied on human labor to complete them.

Visitors returned, and he was advised by divine figures to dwell at *Dōngyáng Fùniú Shān* (East Yang’s Hidden Cow Mountain). Upon arriving, he found an ancient monastery renovated and ready for residence. He practiced the *sānbēn jiǔdào* (three sprints, nine methods) for ten years. Suddenly, a radiance filled his chamber, and a single *dānzhī* (elixir grass) sprouted, striking the stone beneath it and producing a resonant metallic sound. In a dream, a divine person told him: *"Beneath the dripping spring of the mountain behind lies a stone where a golden fish crosses it—you may ascend to heaven with this."*

He was instructed that only this grass striking the stone would summon the fish. Later, he sought it out, and when he struck the stone with the grass, a thunderous force shook the earth. The massive stone cracked open, revealing the golden fish, three *chǐ* in length, which then soared into the sky, surrounded by swirling clouds and mists. The True Person once prayed for his mother’s blessings, placing nine *yōnghuā dēng* (lanterns of the Nine Abysses) in the *Jīn lù bái jiǎn* (golden talismans and white tablets) style, which remains in use to this day. The benefits to the *yōumíng* (netherworld) are immeasurable.

He also authored *The Celestial Pivot of Sun and Moon* and *The Song of Pointing Out Errors*, which circulate in the world.

In the *Xuān Hé* era of the *Shèngsòng* (Revered Song), the monastery was renamed *Xiānyǐn Guān* (Hidden Immortal Monastery), located within the northern city walls of *Chéngdū*.

**Fù Liànshī** (Fù Xiānzōng), styled **Xiānzōng** (Immortal Ancestor), was from *Cháng’ān*. His father, **Lún**, served as the magistrate of *Zīyáng*. **Xiānzōng** from a young age took delight in Daoist learning, thus secluding himself at *Zīyáng Shān* (Resource Yang Mountain). Soon after, a divine person revealed to him that *Yù’àn Shān* (Jade Button Mountain) was suitable for cultivation, so he constructed the *Qiānlíng Guān* (Thousand Autumns Monastery) and resided there for a decade.

One day, several divine figures appeared and said: *"Master, this mountain is our deity. Since you have taken up residence here, we have not known a moment’s peace, let alone this place being a blessed domain. The *Pínggāng Shān* (Flat Ridge Mountain) to the west of the prefecture is where you should dwell."* Heeding their words, the mountain spirits served as his attendants, and he built an altar and chambers at the site.

When Emperor *Mínghuáng* championed the Dao, he summoned **Xiānzōng** to the court. Passing through *Lìzhōu*’s *Jiúpóbó Jīn* (Orange-Bamboo Ferry of Lì Prefecture), water demons plagued the locals. **Xiānzōng** inscribed two stone tablets with talismans and cast them into the water, whereupon two massive fish stranded on the shallows, their bellies bearing the inscription: *"Red carp, red carp, dwelling in river waters, not avoiding the Immortal Officials—your fate is sealed by justice."* The prefectural magistrate reported this, and the emperor decreed the establishment of a shrine for **Xiānzōng** at the ferry.

Upon arriving in the capital, he was assigned to preside over a *jiào* (ritual) at the *Shàngqīng Gōng* (Upper Clarity Palace). The emperor personally attended the altar. When **Xiānzōng** arrived, he requested the presence of the *Qīngtóng Jūn* (Youth Lord of the East) and his officials and attendants. In an instant, celestial soldiers filled the eastern side of the altar, and the emperor was filled with fear.

After the ritual concluded, he asked **Xiānzōng** how he had achieved such power. **Xiānzōng** replied: *"My cultivation focuses solely on pacifying the people and benefiting all things. I maintain a tranquil and unadorned simplicity, clear as still water, undisturbed as a calm mind. Thus, I overcome myself."* The emperor was deeply moved and pleased.

In time, he requested to return to his mountain, and the emperor ordered the expansion of his monastery, personally inscribing the name and renaming it *Yìngzhēn Guān* (Responding to True). On the fourteenth day of the tenth month in the third year of *Qiányuán*, he suddenly heard a voice from the sky: *"The Most High commands your return."* He bathed, ascended his platform, and attained *spiritual dissolution*. Some saw him in *Jiǎnzhōu*, riding a green donkey as he departed—this was surely an instance of *shījiě* (body dissolution).

**Lǘqiū Xiānshēng** (Lǘqiū Fāngyuǎn), styled **Dàfāng** (Great Rectitude), was from *Yùn* (Yun). At sixteen, he mastered the *Classics and Histories*. At twenty-nine, he entered the Dao, studying under **Yóu Yuánzé**.

The Master of the Marsh said to him: *"Have you not heard the Master Lao say, 'My greatest affliction is that I have a body'? Truly, the body arises from non-action (*wuwei*) and gives rise to action (*youwei*); now you return to the root, which is called non-action. Non-action means that when one speaks of 'non-being,' one attains emptiness (*kong*); when one speaks of 'being,' one meets obstruction (*zhe*). Grasping both being and non-being leads to stagnation (*zhi*). Only when you harmonize being and non-being, extinguishing all thought and resting in thoughtlessness (*wu xin*), will you approach the Dao. And indeed, the Master Shakyamuni (释氏) established this as the foundation of the Zen School (禅宗).*

Confucius said: *"The stillness that does not move—its measure is singularity (一)."*

The Master Lao further asked: *"What is that which, when faced, has no front, and when followed, has no back? What is this thing?"*

If you can grasp this in silence, what more do you need to seek? Why must you dwell beneath the long pines of an empty mountain? What is lamentable is that your talent and capacity are sufficient to become a true exemplar for the Daoist School (*Zhenmen*).*

Fāngyuǎn received his teachings and departed, then further studied under **Liú Chǔjìng** and **Yè Zàngzī** for the Daoist initiation (*dàojì*). Admiring **Zhìchuān Zhēnbái** for his upright character, his reputation grew even greater.

The ruler of **Wúyuè** (Wu and Yue), **Qián Liú**, revered his purity and simplicity, visiting him at **Dàdí Dòng** (Great Filtration Cave) and constructing a dwelling for him to reside in.

Emperor **Zhāozōng** repeatedly summoned him in edicts, but he did not attend. The emperor then granted him official robes, bestowing the titles *Miàohǔo Dàshī* (Master of Marvelous Being) and *Yuántóng Xiānshēng* (Master of Original Harmony). His disciples numbered over two hundred, but only a dozen or so truly grasped the essence of cultivating *virtue/power* (*xiūzhēn*) and refining the *qi/spirit* (*liànshén*). Later, one day, he suddenly bathed, sat upright, and attained *spiritual dissolution* (*shījiě*). When his coffin was opened, only an empty casket remained.

**Dù Guāngtíng**, styled **Bīnshèng**, the Daoist Master of the Dù lineage.

For his time, he was a renowned Confucian scholar, yet failing the *million-word essay* examination, he turned to the Dao/Way, becoming a foremost disciple of **Yìng Shì** (Responding Master). He once remarked that the Daoist teachings and rituals, since compiled by **Hàn Tiānshī** (Han Heavenly Master) and **Lù Xiūjìng** (Lu Modesty of the Pure), had over time fallen into disuse and decay. Thus, he scrutinized their authenticity, systematically recording their origins, and so the Daoist clergy across the land followed his arrangements to this day.

Emperor **Lǐzōng** summoned him to serve as a literary draftsman in **Lín Dé Diàn** (Lynx Virtue Hall). At the time, he was praised as saying:
*"A forest of words, a sea of learning;
Upholding the lineage, establishing the teaching—
the foremost under heaven."*

During the **Zhōnglǐ** era, he accompanied the imperial procession to Shu, where he grew old in **Chéngdū**. When **Wáng Jiàn** ruled Shu, he summoned him as a teacher for the royal prince. He once told **Xú Guāngbù** (Xu Broad Virtue), *"In my youth, I studied at the imperial university, where all texts were available. Within a month, I divided each day’s study:
The first day, I recited the Classics;
The second, I read the histories and commentaries;
The third, I practiced composition;
The fourth, I recorded anecdotes;
The fifth, I rested leisurely to cultivate my will.
This cycle completed in five days, repeated monthly.
In less than five years, I mastered all the texts."*

**Guāngbù**, the Shù chancellor, had once been his disciple.

The Heavenly Master first encountered the **Chén Tǐ** (Body of Truth) scripture and later obtained divine elixirs. In **Chéngdū**, he resided at **Zhū Xiān Yīn** (Jade Immortal’s Retreat), where his teachings resonated widely. In autumn, he declined further invitations and never met again. One day, he suddenly told his disciples, *"Last night, I dreamed of presenting myself to the Celestial Sovereign as the overseer of Mín Yuè (the sacred peaks)."* At that time, the **True Palace** was being constructed on **Qīngchéng Shān** (Green City Mountain), and its completion was announced. He then donned his ritual robes, performed farewell rites, and ascended the hall, bidding his disciples farewell before attaining *spiritual dissolution* (*huà*). His remains were buried on **Qīngchéng**, but his coffin was found unusually light—upon opening it, only a single sandal remained.

He authored numerous works, including the *Hùnyuán Tú* (Mixed Primordial Diagram), *Yìjì Shèngfù* (Sacred Ode of the Epoch), *Guǎngshèng Yì* (Expanded Sacred Meaning), *Lìdì Jì* (Record of the Imperial Lineage), *Língyàn Jì* (Record of Miraculous Verifications), *Kējiào Yífàn* (Ritual Standards of Teachings), *Zhāngcí Biǎoshì* (Models of Chapters and Proclamations), and hundreds of songs and miscellaneous writings, collectively titled *Guǎngchéng Jí* (Collection of Broad Achievement). He was posthumously honored as **Guǎngchéng Xiānshēng** (Master of Broad Achievement).

**Sū Chéngyǐn** (Su Concealed Virtue)
The Daoist **Sū Chéngyǐn** resided at **Zhèn Yáng Lóngxīng Guàn** (Dragon’s Ascension Hall in Zhengyang), mastering the teachings of **Lǎozǐ** and **Zhuāngzǐ**, and excelling in *qi* cultivation and nourishment. In the **Kāibǎo** era (968 CE), Emperor **Tàizǔ** stationed in **Zhèn Yáng**, summoned him to the palace. The emperor said, *"Master, you are over eighty yet appear youthful—this is the art of nurturing life. Please instruct me."* **Chéngyǐn** replied, *"My method of nurturing life is no more than refining thought and cultivating the spirit. For rulers, the path differs."* He cited **Lǎozǐ**:
*"If I act without action, the people transform themselves;
If I desire nothing, the people return to simplicity.
Without action, without desire—
the spirit merges with the Great Harmony."*

The emperor praised his words and bestowed extraordinary honors.

**Zhāng Wúmèng** (Zhang Dreamless)
**Zhāng Wúmèng**, styled **Língyǐn** (Hidden Forest), was renowned for his filial piety. He favored solitude, studied the *Yìjīng* (Changes Classic), and at adulthood, entrusted his wealth to his younger brother before entering **Huà Shān** (Flowery Mountain), where he befriended **Zhǒng Fàng** (Seed Release) and **Liú Hǎitán** (Liu Sea Pot), serving **Xīyí Shì** (Harmonious Master). He gained profound insights. Afterward, he wandered to **Tiāntái Shān** (Heavenly Terrace Mountain) and **Chìchéng** (Scarlet City), dwelling there for over a decade. His cultivation was refined, and he expressed his inner truths in poetry, composing *Hái Yuán Piān* (Hundred Verses of Returning to the Primordial) with a hundred stanzas. **Xià Yīnggōng** (Summer Noble Lord) visited him in the mountains, obtaining the poems to present at court. **Wáng Jìgōng** (Wang of Ji), as chancellor, received the poems and later submitted them to the throne.

Emperor **Zhēnzōng** inquired about strategies for longevity. **Wúmèng** replied, *"I am a rustic—only reciting the *Lǎozǐ* and *Zhōuyì* in the mountains."* The emperor commanded him to lecture on the *Yìjīng*, and he expounded on the **Jiǎn** (Modesty) hexagram. The emperor asked, *"Why only the Modesty hexagram?"* **Wúmèng** answered, *"In times of great abundance, one must govern with modesty."* The emperor delighted in his words and offered him the post of **Zhuózhuò Zuǒláng** (Literary Draftsman), which he declined. Later, the emperor summoned him again to lecture on *Hái Yuán Piān*, offering wine and gifts, which he also refused. The emperor then bestowed the title **Chùshì Xiānshēng** (Recluse Master), which he declined as well. The emperor composed a poem in reply:

*"The Dao of Mixed Primordial contains pure essence,
Observe it—no trace, listen—no sound.
Only the enlightened attain this truth,
Adrift beyond the world, immersed in stillness.

Floating clouds unfold beyond ordinary form,
Flowing water circles without fixed shape.
On impulse, I left the mountain’s gate,
To discuss the Dao, I briefly visited the royal court.
With the wind, I heard the essence of the lineage,
Returning to the stone, I sought my natural ease.

Jade and silk, cap and sash—unworthy of my regard,
I sang long and now return with imperial favor.
The next day, I departed by decree,
The court ordered my stipend from Tàizhōu—
I did not request it.
Thus, my life’s end was pure and untainted."*

He died at ninety-nine in **Jīnlíng**. Three days later, white *qi* emerged from his crown, rising three feet high. His *Jūn Tái Shī* (Jade Terrace Poems) circulated in the world. His disciple, **Bìxū Zǐ** (Azure Void Child) **Chén Jǐngyuán** (Chen Scenic Element), inherited the essence of **Lǎozǐ** and **Zhuāngzǐ**.

**Liú Shì** (Master Liu)
**Liú Cóngshàn**, styled **Shùnfū** (Obedient Husband), from a young age, favored Daoist learning. He took ordination at **Jiànlóng Guàn** (Observing Dragon Hall). In the early **Tiānshèng** era, he resided at **Jǐnglíng Gōng** (Scenic Spirit Palace) by imperial decree. The emperor and empress desired to receive Daoist initiation. **Shàoguān Miào Shì** (Mysterious Observation Master) **Zhū Zìyīng** (Zhu Self-Cultivation) established an altar at **Yùqīng Zhāoyìng Gōng** (Jade Purity Responsive Palace), commanding **Cóngshàn** to participate in the ritual. The emperor was strict in filial offerings, sending envoys to instruct him on the taboo dates of the late emperor, ordering him to recite incantations before the deities during the ritual meal.

Thus, **Cóngshàn** compiled the incantation formulas from the **Sāndòng Jīng** (Three Caverns Scriptures) and later submitted the ritual texts. The emperor praised him, bestowing the title **Quánsù** (Complete Purity), and ordered his compositions to be inscribed in all Daoist halls. The ritual of *zòushí* (ritual meal offerings) originated with him. When the **Yánníng Gōng** (Serene Peace Palace) was completed, many submitted poems for the imperial portrait’s five-viscera inscriptions, but only **Cóngshàn’s** met with approval. His text was engraved on gold and jade plaques.

When Emperor **Rénzōng** fell ill, he summoned **Cóngshàn** to present petitions inside the palace, commanding officials to relay his words. After kneeling and presenting his memorial, the emperor asked, *"Did your words reach me?"* He replied, *"They have reached you."*

When the emperor’s passing was near, after but a few moments, he suddenly regained his vitality and clarity, and commanded that it be announced: *"Ask the General Bo of what divine origin?"*
**Cóngshàn** replied: *"Beneath the Three Heavens’ Gate stands a deity—the General Bo of Zhōngyuán, who governs the spirit of petitioning."*

Again, the proclamation came: *"Set up his station."*
The next day, the imperial health fully recovered. He instructed his attendants: *"Last night, I reached the Celestial Gate, where General Bo said, ‘The Emperor has not yet arrived; I must borrow a steed to return you swiftly.’ Thus, I awoke."*

The emperor removed his imperial robes, offering gold and silk in gratitude, and sought to bestow upon him the title of *xiānshēng* (Immortal Master). **Cóngshàn** declined with humility.
In the reign of Emperor **Yīngzōng**, the Chancellor **Hán Wèigōng** (Han of the Wei clan) again petitioned for the title to be granted, but he refused once more.

On the twenty-eighth day of the seventh month of **Xīnníng the Third Year**, after bathing in purification, he gathered his disciples and declared: *"I await the great wind’s arrival, then I shall depart."*
Soon after, the wind arose as foretold, and he ascended in transformation.

Later, a traveler returning from **Shǔ** (Sichuan) reported seeing the Master riding a white horse into the region, with the parting words: *"If you encounter my disciples, convey this message to them."*
Thus, it was known that he had achieved *shījiě* (embodied ascension).

He compiled ritual fasting procedures, methods for petitioning the Dao, and left behind hymns and poems in circulation.

---
**Daoist Canon’s Universal Teachings (Required Texts, Volume I)**
Original Title: *Lǚ Tàigǔ Ji* (Collected Works of Lü the Ancient)
Nine scrolls.
Source: *Zhèngtóng Dàozàng* (Orthodox Daoist Canon), Section One.

---
**Daoist Canon’s Universal Teachings (Required Texts, Volume II)**
*Hèlín Dàoshì Lǚ Tàigǔ Ji* (Collected Works of Lü the Ancient, the Crane Forest Daoist)
*Cí Zàn Piān* (Hymns and Praises)
*Qǐtáng Sòng* (Hymn of the Awakened Hall)

「To cultivate the Dao, one must be diligent and earnest, gathering sincerity and refining the elixir of truth.
Burn incense to honor the *Tàishàng Lǎojiūn* (Supreme Venerable),
where the *zhēnqì* (true *qi*) mingles with fragrant smoke.
Only may the Great Compassion be opened,
as the Seventh Patriarch departs from the shadowed realm.
**Hymn of the Offerings**
The *Xuánxī* (Suspended Pivot) stars turn in their course,
the *Yùlòu* (jade water clock) chimes its first resonance.
Having conveyed the offerings to the True Officials,
with devout sincerity, the *qiè* (sacrificial) feast is now begun.
With earnest words, I pray to the *shèmàn* (wild tribes of the south),
my revelation all the more focused and refined.
Gazing upward toward the multitude of True Immortals,
they seem to descend from the Ninth Heaven in faint outline.

**Hymn of Wisdom**
Wisdom arises from the root of *jiè* (precepts),
and the True Dao finds its master in precepts.
From these Three Treasures, all flourishes,
as the Highly Authentic ones revere and accept.
This vessel of non-perishing traverses boundless seas,
in a flash, it crosses the Great Void.
At this moment of preaching precepts,
all the heavens come to pay homage with folded hands.
**Hymn of Revering Precepts**
The Dao is the school of the *wúxīn* (heartless/non-dual) principle,
and all things become fields of merit.
The rewards of deeds are without fixed master,
for each is born from their own original vows.
To empty oneself for all beings,
to pour one’s heart out—none may be excluded.
The Great Sage upholds the utmost teachings,
just as the heavens are nourished by rain.
The lofty peaks are never left unvisited,
yet the humble valleys become profound depths.
The sea is king of all streams,
yet it willingly sheds its dragon scales.
Through countless *jié* (kalpas), wisdom is preserved,
not merely confined to a single age.
To revere precepts brings no loss,
through all lifetimes, one sows good connections.
With focused contemplation, I aspire to the Great Vehicle,
to ultimately embody the True Dao.

**Hymn of Inviting the Master**
All should show reverence.
In ancient rites, inviting the Master refers only to the Three Masters—*Scripture*, *Canon*, and *Transmission*—
and threefold invocation is made.
Even before the proper altar is established to honor the Master’s presence,
it is the *self*-transmitted Three Masters of the Three Worlds.
Later generations failed to examine this closely,
mistaking the Three Masters for celestial Daoist officials,
thus adding them to the Five Masters.
Since this is now the case,
it cannot be altered again—
let the Three Masters among the Five be honored as:
*Yùluóqiào Zhēnrén* (Idyllicly Elevated True Person),
*Zhēndìngguāng Zhēnrén* (True Person of Illuminating Stability),
and *Guāngmiàoyīn Zhēnrén* (True Person of Resplendent Sound).
These are the Three Masters who witnessed the *Scripture* on Tiantai,
the ancestral teachers of transmission,
never forgetting their origins.

As for the *Sānián* (Three Sovereigns),
they are also called the Three Masters,
already revered in the proper altar rites—
they cannot be reduced to the Five Masters.

In the *Xuánzhōng* (Mysterious Central) hierarchy,
the first rank belongs to the Master,
followed by the Three Masters,
then the *Jiānyàn* (Supervising Feast) Grandmasters.
**For rites of fasting and Daoist practice:**
Invite the *Xuánzhōng Dàfǎshī* (Grandmaster of the Mysterious Central) to descend and preside.
**For rites of fasting and Daoist practice:**
Invite the Three Masters—*Scripture*, *Canon*, and *Transmission*—to descend and preside.
**For rites of fasting and Daoist practice:**
Invite the *Jiānyàn Dàfǎshī* (Grandmaster Supervising the Feast) to descend and preside.

When the *yún yǔ* (cloud chariot) has descended,
and the *hè jià* (crane carriage) arrives,
the feast is complete in all its rounds—
then it is time to offer farewell.

**Singing the Daoist Praises**
All assembled at the *Dàocháng* (Daoist Hall),
each focusing their hearts,
united in harmonious reverence,
all Three Treasures invoked in prayer.

**Praise of the Chinese Realm**
To study speech and to study conduct—
both are *xuéyán* (learning of words).」

Thus, the Master of the **Scripture** takes precedence,
the **Canon** and **Transmission** Masters follow next,
and the **Jiānyàn Dàfǎshī** (Grandmaster Supervising the Feast) ranks below them.

**For Daoist fasting and practice:**
The **Mysterious Central** Grandmaster is revered as the **Léfǎ** (Law of Music),
and the **Scripture** is cherished like pearls and jade.
With **precepts** held firm and the **Six Emotions** subdued,
one recites the **Dao/Way** to dispel all cravings.
In **dampness and stillness**, the **orthodox qi** is stilled,
and in **serene silence**, the spirit finds repose.
Both **celestial demons** and **earthly spirits** are honored and protected,
so that in this life and the next, one attains **great blessings**.

The **Chinese Realm** flourishes in **profound harmony**,
and the **Scripture** and **Dao/Way** thrive in splendor.
Heaven and man share the same aspiration,
and **Lofty and Mysterious** enters the **Great Vehicle**.

**Establishing the Field of Merit through the Mind**,
the **Dharma Wheel** ascends without end.
The **Seven Ancestors** are born in the **Celestial Hall**,
and my body soars like the **White Sun**.

The **Great Dao/Way** penetrates the **Mysterious and Profound**,
and with every thought, none fails to resonate.
Refining the essence, one attains **Immortal Truth**,
and thus becomes a **Golden Body** (Vajra-like).

To **transcend and guide** the **Three Realms** is difficult,
yet the **Five Torments** of the **Underworld** are dissolved.
All return to the **Scripture of the Most High**,
and with every recitation, one prostrates in homage.

**Ten Verses of the Jade Capital (Yùjīng) on Lofty and Mysterious (Xūwú)**
With prostrations to the **Most High**,
incense is burned to return to **Emptiness**.
The **radiant light** follows me back,
and the **Dharma Wheel** revolves three times.
**Mysterious Aspirations** flourish in the **Four Great Elements**,
and **spiritual rejoicing** extends to **kings and nobles**.
The **Seven Ancestors** are born in the **Celestial Hall**,
their **resplendent brilliance** spreading far and wide.

**Singing and dancing** in the **Great Desert’s** vastness,
the **Heavenly Music** delights me in its harmony.
The **fragrance** of the **Supreme Virtue** is unmatched,
and **lower immortals** cannot compare.
**Wondrous thoughts** awaken **profound awareness**,
and **serene** movements traverse **Emptiness**.
With **swift steps** along the **cloudly cords**,
one rides the **Void** and walks the **Mysterious Path**.

**Reciting** to the **Sovereign of Unity**,
all **passes** are naturally regulated.
Gazing downward, one commands the **Eight Seas** to tremble,
and upward, one ascends with **High Immortals**.
The **Heavens** scatter **incense and flowers**,
and the **serene spirit-wind** stirs.
**Past aspirations** are rooted in **destiny’s foundation**,
thus achieving **Lofty and Mysterious** emulation.

With **joy** before the **Most High**,
even **ten thousand kalpas** are but the beginning.
**Majestic** is the **Mysterious Capital Mountain**,
the **Ten Directions** all revere the **Imperial One**.

**Dazzling** is the **Celestial Treasure Platform**,
its **radiant flames** flowing like the sun.
**Gleaming** is the **Jade Forest’s** splendor,
and **clustered** are the **Seven Treasures** of the **Luminous Grove**.
Ever **nourishing** the **Essential Precision**,
one refines the **elixir** to solidify the **form and substance**.
**Golden Light** scatters across **Purple Micro**,
and **Lofty and Mysterious** ascends in **effortless grace**.

Gazing downward and upward, one reveres the **Most High**,
and the **Jade Capital’s** brilliance adorns the **Dan Tian** (Elestial Field).
To the left, one raises the **Idyllic Ritual**,
and to the right, one embraces the **Jade Luminaries**.
With the **Six Perfections**, one observes **Brahman’s conduct**,
and **Daoist Virtue** renews itself daily.
**Past lives’** accumulated **merit** manifests,
and hearing the **Scripture** feels like encountering a **kin**.
The **Heavenly Sovereign** elevates **great talent**,
and one recites **sacred texts** with **profound reverence**.

**Orthodox qi** flows in **Great Harmony**,
and one **inhales and exhales** the **Luminous Elixir**.
**Embryonic Breathing** calms the **Hundred Passes**,
and **Lofty and Serene** explores the **Three Treasures’** essence.
The **Earthly Pill** shines with **illuminating clarity**,
and thus one becomes the **Jade-Hued Immortal**.

The **Demon King** respects and receives this,
so one may **audience the Heavens**.
All begin with **fasting and precepts**,
and through **accumulated merit**, past **karmic ties** are fulfilled.

**Soaring** in the **Great Void**,
one **ascends** with the **Highest Immortals**.
With **reins in hand**, one traverses the **Ten Directions**,
and in **swift rotation**, one rests in the **Mysterious and Profound**.

Gazing upward, one beholds the **Effulgent Platform of the Kalpa**,
and downward, one surveys the **Purple Cloud Array**.
**Adrift in Lofty and Mysterious**,
one sits together on the **Lotus Flower**.

Through **accumulated learning**, one becomes a **True Person**,
and in **serene composure**, the **vital energies** harmonize.
**Endlessly** enjoying **boundless longevity**,
what need is there for **ten thousand autumns**?

The **Great Dao/Way**’s **Master** is **Mysterious and Profound**,
and **True Immortals** possess **unfathomable brilliance**.
The **Prince** transmits **spiritual talismans**,
and **Taiyi** (Great Unity) presents **illuminating scrolls**.
The **Sacred Relics** gleam in **golden splendor**,
and the **Dragon Chariot** swiftly comes to welcome.

The **Heavenly Sovereign** gazes from the **clouds**,
and **floating**, one rides the **Void**.
**Incense and flowers** fall like **flying snow**,
and **abundant** **spiritual winds** adorn the **Mysterious Beams**.

With **head and hands** in homage to the **Golden Gate**,
one **clasps hands** and **wanders** in the **Jade Capital**.
**Circular trees** enclose the **Garden of Radiance**,
and **dazzling** is the **Seven Treasures Forest**.
**Heavenly beasts** number in the **thousands**,
with **Lions** vast in the **ten thousand leagues**.
**Flying Dragons** pace and **roar**,
and the **Divine Phoenix** responds with **melodic chirps**.

**Spirit-winds** fan **wondrous flowers**,
and **pure fragrance** scatters across the **human breast**.
Without **Lofty and Mysterious talent**,
how could one **attain this necessity**?

**Admonish** my **Nine Dragon Chariot**,
and ride the **Void** in **effortless grace**.
The **Eight Heavens** are as near as **one’s fingertips**,
and the **Six Harmonies** are but a **brief span**.
The **multitude of Immortals** recite **sacred texts**,
while the **Most High** sings **pure melodies**.
**Incense and flowers** drift with the **wind**,
and **jade-like sounds** rise to the **Purple Expanse**.

The **Five Torments** burst forth at once,
and the **Eight Difficulties** are overcome by the **Scripture’s** vastness.
**Wondrous** indeed is the **Enclosure of Spirit-Treasures**,
and this **Great Law** is the **Bridge of the Dao/Way**.

The **Celestial Hall of Unity**,
**vague and bright** in its **spiritual radiance**,
the **Dharma Wheel’s** **cord** revolves,
and **Void** enters **formlessness**.

The **Void Sovereign** strokes the **cloudly jade**,
while the **multitude of True Ones** recite **sacred texts**.
**High Immortals** extend their **palms** in praise,
and **through kalpas** they safeguard the **Sacred Body**.

**Absolute Truth** awaits nothing,
yet at times one **guides the flying Dragon**.
**Long fasting** gathers in the **Mysterious Capital**,
and **jade chimes** strike the **Lotus Bell**.

**Ten thousand Immortals** assemble at the **Heavenly Sovereign’s** abode,
their **flying sandals** stepping on the **cloudly roots**.
**Misty** like **fine dew**,
**gradually** they trail **filmy robes**.
**Wondrous** and **light**, they follow **auspicious clouds**,
and **graceful**, they ride the **colorful phoenix**.

Near **accompanying** the **Jade Pool’s** feast,
suddenly one is **pointed** to return to the **Mysterious Heaven**.
Standing still at the **Firmament’s** shore,
one **ascends** to the **radiance of the Sun Sovereign**.

With **swift steps** along the **cloudly cords**,
the **heavenly wind** **rustles** and blows.
**Floating** in the **handle of the Dipper**,
one **holds the broom** and **salutes the celestial flags**,
the **lion** **adorns** the **red sash**,
and the **qilin** leads the **emerald carriage**.

**Soaring** around the **Eight Extremes**,
almost **witnessing** the **chestnut branches** bloom.
**Green locks** cascade in **cloudlike chignons**,
and **blue mists** weave **feathered robes**.
In the **morning**, one **proceeds** to the **Hall of Yang Virtue**,
and at **night**, one **visits** the **Moonlight Gate**.
**Fanning and stirring** the **circular heavenly fire**,
one **conceals and stores** the **spirit of the Sixteen Machines**.

The **Jade Chamber** cannot **detain**,
and one **returns** to the **Nine Heavens** to **fly**.

The **White Crane Hymns**

**White Crane** at first was born in **Purple Forbidden**,
and now **dwells** in the **Celestial Abode** to nurture **feathered robes**.
**Asking** the **Daoist Immortal** when **one shall depart**,
**do not say** one **cannot** **accompany** the **clouds** in flight.

The **White Crane** returns to the **Nine Heavens** after **thousand springs**,
while **mountains and rivers** remain unchanged—**mortals** are not.
Had it not been for the **Clear Proclamation** of **Ding Lingwei**,
who would **recognize** the **White Crane** of old?

The **White Crane** **flies** down from the **Nine Heavens**,
its **clear calls** **piercing** through **auspicious mists**.
The **sun and moon** **urge** one another—**mortals** age swiftly,
yet **better** to **cultivate the Dao** and **learn from the Immortals**.

The **Virtuous Sovereign of Great Unity** has a **snow-white visage**,
**Soaring in the Void**, coming and going with **no trace**.
**Penglai** must be **sought**—and now **one goes**,
while the **qilin** **stands** at the window, the **crane** among the **pines**.

The **White Crane**, born of **Heaven**, has a **long lifespan**,
**soaring** in the **Immortal Realm**, attending the **Void Sovereign**.
When **thousand springs** arrive at the **Clear Proclamation**,
**one returns** to the **Nine Heavens**, the **Natural Homeland**.

The **White Crane** **flies** in the **Jade Capital**,
**traversing** the **Three Realms**, **manifesting** **Eternal Life**.
If **cultivation** reaches the **Immortal Realm**,
**one shall ride** the **True Vehicle** into the **Cloud Court**.

---

**White Crane Hymns**
The **White Crane**, **congealed** in **frost**, wears a **crimson crest**,
**Ever dwelling** in the **Empty Verdant** **withdrawn** in mystery.
The **Three Pure Ones** **love** this **place of carefree ease**,
for **Heavenly** and **Earthly** affairs are **not the same**.

---

**White Crane Hymns**
At the **Eight Scenic** **period**, **ascend** to the **Forbidden Palace**,
and the **Nine Pure Ones** **bestow blessings** with the **Auspicious Scriptures**.
Once **one spoke** of **playful antics** and **gazed** upon **Immortal Feathers**,
and **under the fierce sun**, **one lingered** in the **Court of Fortune**.

---

**White Crane Hymns**
**Incubated** and **transformed**, the **Soulbird** **calls** from the **Nine Heavens**,
with **snow-white plumage** and **crimson crest**—both **radiant**.
**Mortals**, **do not mistake** this **return** to the **Clear Proclamation**,
for it **brings auspicious omens**—**prosperity** for **ten thousand years**.

---

**Hymn of Departure**
**The Dao** **begins** with **fasting**,
**diligent practice** leads **one** to the **Golden Gate**.

---

**The Music of the Jade Purity**
In the **Purple Pure** **Heavens**, the **Flowery Forest** **nurtures** life,
where the **Crimson Realms** and **Jade Branches** **hide** deep **bamboo leaves**.
**Chewing** and **savoring** **abundant blossoms**, **one’s body** **does not age**,
**Gazing downward**, **one observes** the **Black Hare** **changing** **light and shadow**.

The **Original Sovereign** is **known** as the **Eight Qi** **Green Spirit**,
with **brocade robes** **fluttering** in **flying skirts**, **dwelling** in the **Jade City**.
**Holding** the **Imperial Talisman**, **one governs** the **Daoist Register**,
**Removing** **dust and filth**, **one aids** the **multitude of living beings**.

In the **Nine-Day Palace**, the **Four Elderly Immortals** **gather**,
and at the **Mountain of Broad Mists**, **one feasts** the **Celestial Guests**.
**Resounding bells** and **plucked strings** **move** the **Spiritual Wine**,
while the **Empty Verdant** **melts** in warmth—**another spring** **emerges**.

---

**The Music of the Supreme Purity**
The **Original Sovereign of Great Unity** **commands** the **ranked Immortals**,
with **scarlet radiance** and **crimson hues** **illuminating** the **Cinnabar Fields**.
**Perfect merit** **encounters** **those who erase** the **Dark Register**,
and **one awaits** the **Laughing Scholar of Hongya** **to clap the shoulder**.

Behind the **Golden Gate**, the **Luminous Sovereign** **shines**,
**Emitting essence**, **one’s brilliance** **forms** the **Cinnabar Clouds**.
Had it not been for the **Supreme Sage** **passing on** the **transmission**,
how could **mortals** possess the **Jade Texts**?

At **midnight**, the **Five Nodes** **burn** with **pure incense**,
and **Heavenly** and **Human** **Immortal Maidens** all **hear** from afar.
**Flavors** and **breaths** **harmonize**, **one responds** in **unison**,
as the **Crimson Talismans** and **Rainbow Banners** **descend** from the **Five Clouds**.

---
